# Windows 10: Manage and Maintain Windows 10

> Extend the life of the Windows machines in your organization by learning how to perform basic management and maintenance of Windows 10. Learn how to configure updates, monitor events and performance, back up and restore files, recover the entire system, and configure OneDrive for Business. She touches on Windows Defender, System Restore, Windows Insider, Resource Monitor, and more obscure servicin

> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019) | 2h 22m | Intermediate | 28K learners

#### The benefits of managing and maintaining Windows 10

#### Configure basic Windows Update options

>
> **[0:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/configure-basic-windows-update-options?u=76281980&t=3)** Windows Update is a service that provides important updates to Microsoft operating systems, protects against malware and security exploits, enhances Windows components and improves functionality.

> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/configure-basic-windows-update-options?u=76281980&t=15)** Windows Update has been available to users in control panel since Windows Vista.

>

>
> **[2:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/configure-basic-windows-update-options?u=76281980&t=122)** This feature creates a local cache of updates and shares those with other PCs on your network.
>
> **[2:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/configure-basic-windows-update-options?u=76281980&t=128)** You can enable it for your local network or internet.
>

>
> **[2:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/configure-basic-windows-update-options?u=76281980&t=141)** Not all the options about Windows Update have to do with updates.
>

>
> **[2:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/configure-basic-windows-update-options?u=76281980&t=153)** I'll type gpedit.msc and select edit group policy in the results.
>
> **[2:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/configure-basic-windows-update-options?u=76281980&t=161)** Local group policies are rules that you enable or disable that determine how the computer will work and what you allow users to do and can be used to place restrictions on the various Windows components like Windows Updates, as well as what you'll allow your users to do, well, on the computer.
>
> **[2:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/configure-basic-windows-update-options?u=76281980&t=179)** There are two areas to consider, computer configuration and user configuration, because I want to apply changes to the computer in this instance, I'll expand computer configuration and navigate to this settings, computer configuration, administrative templates, Windows components, and down at the bottom Windows update.
>
> **[3:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/configure-basic-windows-update-options?u=76281980&t=205)** If you're interested in controlling how Windows Updates work you might want to read through the options, you might want to, for instance, allow updates to be downloaded automatically over metered connections, to keep mobile users updated, even if they don't have access to wifi.
>
> **[3:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/configure-basic-windows-update-options?u=76281980&t=221)** Perhaps you don't want to include device drivers with Windows Updates because you want to test all drivers first in the lab.
>

>

>

#### Plan for Windows Update in an enterprise
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/plan-for-windows-update-in-an-enterprise?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/plan-for-windows-update-in-an-enterprise?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Narrator] Managing updates on a personal computer or a small group of computers in a network doesn't generally require too much preparation.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/plan-for-windows-update-in-an-enterprise?u=76281980&t=9)** Often you set the update options and let the updates install automatically.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/plan-for-windows-update-in-an-enterprise?u=76281980&t=14)** Keeping computers updated in an enterprise is a lot more complicated than keeping a handful of machines up to date in a small network.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/plan-for-windows-update-in-an-enterprise?u=76281980&t=22)** There are many things to consider prior to installing updates, when thousands of computers are involved, especially when those computers are required for a corporation to run smoothly.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/plan-for-windows-update-in-an-enterprise?u=76281980&t=33)** And when downtime isn't an option.
>
> **[0:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/plan-for-windows-update-in-an-enterprise?u=76281980&t=36)** To make sure things go well during updates, especially big ones like updating from Windows 10 to Windows 11 enterprises create and follow a deployment plan.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/plan-for-windows-update-in-an-enterprise?u=76281980&t=46)** This plan has many parts.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/plan-for-windows-update-in-an-enterprise?u=76281980&t=49)** It will categorize the computers that are already hardware ready for the update.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/plan-for-windows-update-in-an-enterprise?u=76281980&t=54)** It will also define what to do with those that aren't.
>
> **[0:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/plan-for-windows-update-in-an-enterprise?u=76281980&t=57)** An enterprise might skip these machines or relegate them to a lab or other non-essential area, but more often we'll either update or retire them.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/plan-for-windows-update-in-an-enterprise?u=76281980&t=67)** The plan will also calculate software costs based on how many managed and unmanaged devices require the update.
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/plan-for-windows-update-in-an-enterprise?u=76281980&t=75)** This is where servicing plans come into play, something you'll learn about in the next movie.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/plan-for-windows-update-in-an-enterprise?u=76281980&t=81)** Users who bring their own devices will also need those devices to be assessed.
>
> **[1:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/plan-for-windows-update-in-an-enterprise?u=76281980&t=87)** It will also define how to test existing applications to make sure they'll work after the update and what to do if essential apps aren't update ready.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/plan-for-windows-update-in-an-enterprise?u=76281980&t=101)** Here's some of the apps that will need to be assessed.
>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/plan-for-windows-update-in-an-enterprise?u=76281980&t=108)** The enterprise will also have to make sure the existing infrastructure is able to push out the upgrade while also backing up all the data and computers beforehand, you will need to define which updates will be deployed and which will not.
>
> **[2:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/plan-for-windows-update-in-an-enterprise?u=76281980&t=122)** There are many types, including quality and feature updates and the life cycles of each to consider.
>
> **[2:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/plan-for-windows-update-in-an-enterprise?u=76281980&t=129)** And one last thing, the enterprise must define a plan for educating end users on the changes included in the update.
>
> **[2:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/plan-for-windows-update-in-an-enterprise?u=76281980&t=137)** If the update is an entire upgrade to the operating system, those changes could be challenging for those users to find an adapt to.
>
> **[2:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/plan-for-windows-update-in-an-enterprise?u=76281980&t=146)** Once the enterprise has created the plan, they then turned to huddle, do it.
>
> **[2:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/plan-for-windows-update-in-an-enterprise?u=76281980&t=150)** They define what kind of infrastructure they'll use for the deployment and the options vary or are dependent on the enterprise.
>
> **[2:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/plan-for-windows-update-in-an-enterprise?u=76281980&t=158)** Here are only a few of the available options.
>
> **[2:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/plan-for-windows-update-in-an-enterprise?u=76281980&t=162)** It's also important to follow the advice from Microsoft to join Windows insider for business, which I'll discuss later in this course, there are options to preview builds and download and deploy builds from Microsoft's ISO pages when you do.
>
> **[2:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/plan-for-windows-update-in-an-enterprise?u=76281980&t=178)** Finally, there are additional tools for helping an enterprise determine readiness prior to deploying a pilot update, such as those available in Microsoft endpoint manager.
>
> **[3:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/plan-for-windows-update-in-an-enterprise?u=76281980&t=189)** The last part of the deployment plan will include a plan for pilot rollout.
>
> **[3:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/plan-for-windows-update-in-an-enterprise?u=76281980&t=195)** At a high level, the plan will choose a small group of users or devices to receive the upgrade.
>
> **[3:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/plan-for-windows-update-in-an-enterprise?u=76281980&t=202)** They'll implement various updates one at a time when they test.
>
> **[3:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/plan-for-windows-update-in-an-enterprise?u=76281980&t=207)** They'll validate that any deployment processes have succeeded, they'll test and support the users and devices in the pilot, and finally make adjustments and decisions for future updates based on the results of the pilot.
>
> **[3:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/plan-for-windows-update-in-an-enterprise?u=76281980&t=223)** This process can take months to complete the first time, but after it's done, the enterprise can reuse and tweak the plan for future updates.
>
> **[3:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/plan-for-windows-update-in-an-enterprise?u=76281980&t=231)** The takeaway is that a deployment plan is critical to a successful update rollout.

> **[3:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/update-microsoft-store-apps?u=76281980&t=202)** If you ever decide you need to reinstall an app, all you have to do is search for it from the Store.
>
> **[3:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/update-microsoft-store-apps?u=76281980&t=208)** We'll go back Home in the Store and we'll search for Candy Crush.
>
> **[3:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/update-microsoft-store-apps?u=76281980&t=215)** And here we go.
>
> **[3:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/update-microsoft-store-apps?u=76281980&t=216)** It says Owned.
>
> **[3:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/update-microsoft-store-apps?u=76281980&t=218)** I can click and opt to install.
>
> **[3:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/update-microsoft-store-apps?u=76281980&t=222)** If you use Store apps, remember it's best in most cases to let those apps update themselves automatically.
>
> **[3:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/update-microsoft-store-apps?u=76281980&t=229)** However, you're in control and can disable this behavior and uninstall and reinstall apps as desired.

#### Configure event subscriptions
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/configure-event-subscriptions?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/configure-event-subscriptions?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Event viewer logs display events that occur on your computer.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/configure-event-subscriptions?u=76281980&t=5)** Events are created automatically by Windows in response to incidents that occur on your machine, such as an application freezing up, a user trying to log in, or a device driver failing to load, among other things.
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/configure-event-subscriptions?u=76281980&t=19)** I'll expand Windows Logs and choose Application to show you some examples.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/configure-event-subscriptions?u=76281980&t=27)** There's no efficient way to review these logs regularly.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/configure-event-subscriptions?u=76281980&t=30)** There are thousands of events just on the single computer.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/configure-event-subscriptions?u=76281980&t=34)** That's where event subscriptions come in.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/configure-event-subscriptions?u=76281980&t=38)** You can create a subscription to alert you when a specific event occurs on a computer.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/configure-event-subscriptions?u=76281980&t=44)** And you can even have task scheduler perform a task in response to it if you like.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/configure-event-subscriptions?u=76281980&t=49)** Take a little time to review the logs from event viewer and make a list of events you'd like to monitor.
>
> **[0:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/configure-event-subscriptions?u=76281980&t=56)** When you create your first subscription you can refer to that list to make sure you collect exactly what you want.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/configure-event-subscriptions?u=76281980&t=62)** You might want to monitor critical system events, for instance.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/configure-event-subscriptions?u=76281980&t=67)** In event viewer, click subscriptions.
>
> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/configure-event-subscriptions?u=76281980&t=71)** If you are prompted to enable any services, do so and restart your computer if prompted.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/configure-event-subscriptions?u=76281980&t=79)** There are two types of event subscriptions, collector initiated and source computer initiated.
>
> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/configure-event-subscriptions?u=76281980&t=86)** Collector subscriptions are those that retrieve events from another computer.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/configure-event-subscriptions?u=76281980&t=91)** That other computer is called a source computer because it is the source of the events.
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/configure-event-subscriptions?u=76281980&t=97)** This type of subscription is best for smaller networks, because each computer has to be configured manually for it to work.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/configure-event-subscriptions?u=76281980&t=105)** And it would be harder to implement if you had a lot of computers to manage.
>
> **[1:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/configure-event-subscriptions?u=76281980&t=109)** Source computer initiated subscriptions are those that start at the source computer.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/configure-event-subscriptions?u=76281980&t=115)** The source computer sends events to a collector computer.
>
> **[1:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/configure-event-subscriptions?u=76281980&t=119)** This is best for larger networks because source computers can be configured using group policy and do not need to be configured one at a time.
>
> **[2:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/configure-event-subscriptions?u=76281980&t=128)** Whatever you choose, both the source computer and the collector computer need to be configured before any events can be collected.
>
> **[2:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/configure-event-subscriptions?u=76281980&t=136)** Source computers need to run the Windows Remote Management Service and collector computers need to run the Windows Event Collector Service.
>
> **[2:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/configure-event-subscriptions?u=76281980&t=145)** Let's configure the collector computer first.
>
> **[2:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/configure-event-subscriptions?u=76281980&t=148)** We need to enable this computer to view subscriptions.
>
> **[2:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/configure-event-subscriptions?u=76281980&t=152)** I'll do this on my Windows 10 Enterprise computer.
>
> **[2:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/configure-event-subscriptions?u=76281980&t=157)** First we'll open an elevated command prompt.
>
> **[2:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/configure-event-subscriptions?u=76281980&t=162)** I'll type C-M-D.
>
> **[2:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/configure-event-subscriptions?u=76281980&t=164)** I'll right click the command prompt and choose run as administrator.
>
> **[2:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/configure-event-subscriptions?u=76281980&t=172)** Now we need to type the proper command.
>
> **[2:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/configure-event-subscriptions?u=76281980&t=175)** The command is wecutil space qc.
>
> **[3:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/configure-event-subscriptions?u=76281980&t=182)** This is the Windows Event Collector Utility.
>
> **[3:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/configure-event-subscriptions?u=76281980&t=186)** And qc means quick config.
>
> **[3:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/configure-event-subscriptions?u=76281980&t=191)** Would I like to proceed?
>
> **[3:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/configure-event-subscriptions?u=76281980&t=192)** Yes, I'll type y and press enter.
>
> **[3:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/configure-event-subscriptions?u=76281980&t=196)** You can see the Windows Event Collectors Service has been configured successfully.
>
> **[3:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/configure-event-subscriptions?u=76281980&t=201)** Now I'll switch over to my source computer.
>
> **[3:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/configure-event-subscriptions?u=76281980&t=204)** It needs to be configured as well.
>

>

>
> **[3:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/configure-event-subscriptions?u=76281980&t=221)** That command is winrm space quick config.
>
> **[3:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/configure-event-subscriptions?u=76281980&t=226)** Winrm stands for Windows Remote Management and starts the service.
>
> **[3:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/configure-event-subscriptions?u=76281980&t=239)** It says it's not set up yet but would I like to make the changes.

>
> **[4:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/configure-event-subscriptions?u=76281980&t=245)** If your network is set to public, you'll receive an error.

>
> **[4:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/configure-event-subscriptions?u=76281980&t=257)** If other problems are detected, type y to let Windows resolve them.

> **[6:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/manage-performance-with-task-manager?u=76281980&t=377)** The next time you need to diagnose problems with your PC's performance, start with Task Manager.
>
> **[6:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/manage-performance-with-task-manager?u=76281980&t=383)** Its user interface is easy to use, and the graphs and various tabs often make it simple to draw conclusions about what's causing performance issues.

#### Manage performance with Reliability Monitor
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/manage-performance-with-reliability-monitor?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/manage-performance-with-reliability-monitor?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Reliability Monitor,, lets you review the status and stability of your computer system for the longterm.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/manage-performance-with-reliability-monitor?u=76281980&t=7)** As you can see here, Reliability Monitor runs in the background and keeps track of events, software, hardware failures, Windows failures, and more.
>

#### Schedule tasks with Task Scheduler
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/schedule-tasks-with-task-scheduler?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/schedule-tasks-with-task-scheduler?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] If you ever need a program to run a response to an event, you can use Task Scheduler to create a task to perform that action for you automatically.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/schedule-tasks-with-task-scheduler?u=76281980&t=9)** For instance, you can have specific programs start when you log on.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/schedule-tasks-with-task-scheduler?u=76281980&t=14)** Logging on is the event or trigger, and the programs you opt to start are the response to that event.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/schedule-tasks-with-task-scheduler?u=76281980&t=21)** You can also use an event like a full disk error to trigger an action such as running Disk cleanup.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/schedule-tasks-with-task-scheduler?u=76281980&t=26)** You can look for events in Event Viewer, as well, such as unexpected system shutdown errors and perform an action when that happens.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/schedule-tasks-with-task-scheduler?u=76281980&t=35)** You might want to create and save a log file, for example, or run a script you've written.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/schedule-tasks-with-task-scheduler?u=76281980&t=40)** These actions and others can be created, managed, and monitored in Task Scheduler.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/schedule-tasks-with-task-scheduler?u=76281980&t=46)** You can access Task Scheduler from the Computer Management window or using any of these options.
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/schedule-tasks-with-task-scheduler?u=76281980&t=53)** You could search for it.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/schedule-tasks-with-task-scheduler?u=76281980&t=54)** Type taskschd.msc in the search window, or use the scheduled task command at a command prompt.
>
> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/schedule-tasks-with-task-scheduler?u=76281980&t=63)** The simplest way, I think, is to type Task Scheduler.
>
> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/schedule-tasks-with-task-scheduler?u=76281980&t=71)** I already have a lot of scheduled tasks, but I'm going to show you how to create one from scratch.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/schedule-tasks-with-task-scheduler?u=76281980&t=76)** This is the best way to get familiar with Task Scheduler.
>
> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/schedule-tasks-with-task-scheduler?u=76281980&t=80)** When you do this, you can explore all the possibilities for triggers, actions, conditions, and settings.
>
> **[1:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/schedule-tasks-with-task-scheduler?u=76281980&t=87)** Before we start though, let's look at each of those words one more time in more detail.
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/schedule-tasks-with-task-scheduler?u=76281980&t=92)** A trigger is what causes a task to run.
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/schedule-tasks-with-task-scheduler?u=76281980&t=95)** For example, a specific time of day can be configured to trigger an action.
>
> **[1:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/schedule-tasks-with-task-scheduler?u=76281980&t=100)** A trigger can also be an event that was logged in Event Viewer, such as when someone logs on or off the computer.
>
> **[1:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/schedule-tasks-with-task-scheduler?u=76281980&t=107)** Conditions can be added to triggers to further defined when a task will run.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/schedule-tasks-with-task-scheduler?u=76281980&t=111)** While a trigger might set off a test to run on a specific day and time, a condition could require that the computer be idle before it will start.
>
> **[2:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/schedule-tasks-with-task-scheduler?u=76281980&t=120)** An action is what happens when that trigger plus conditions are met and action might mean running a log on or log off script or starting an application like Microsoft Outlook or disc defragmenter.
>
> **[2:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/schedule-tasks-with-task-scheduler?u=76281980&t=133)** A setting affects how a task performs and what happens if it can't run. A setting can be configured to retry the task at a later time, for instance, or to be canceled altogether. To create a task, click create task in the right pane.
>
> **[2:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/schedule-tasks-with-task-scheduler?u=76281980&t=149)** Here. I have my options.

#### Implement encryption

> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/implement-encryption?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Narrator] Encryption is the process of converting data into code.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/implement-encryption?u=76281980&t=4)** And is used to prevent unauthorized access to both data and entire drives.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/implement-encryption?u=76281980&t=9)** Encryption uses keys to lock and unlock the data and both keys must be available for access.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/implement-encryption?u=76281980&t=16)** You can enable basic encryption on all Windows operating systems.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/implement-encryption?u=76281980&t=20)** And you can use BitLocker on Windows Pro, Enterprise and Education.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/implement-encryption?u=76281980&t=26)** Basic encryption can be applied by right clicking a file or folder and choosing the encryption option.
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/implement-encryption?u=76281980&t=32)** This is the type of encryption general home users apply.

> **[4:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/implement-encryption?u=76281980&t=272)** Having your drive encrypted will protect it from unauthorized users, and will prevent access to the data on it, even if someone removes the drive from your computer and installs it in another.

> [!info]- Semantic Content
>
> **Code Keywords:** let (2), protected (1), module (1), finally, (1)
> **Env Vars:** usb (3), tpm (1)
> **Definitions:** is called (1), is a  (1)
> **CLI Commands:** make (1)

>
> **[3:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/create-a-workgroup-or-join-a-domain-14308478?u=76281980&t=238)** Remember, there are several solutions for networking computers.

> **[2:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/manage-users-with-computer-management-and-group-policy?u=76281980&t=125)** It would be quite complicated to manage them all singly in this way, at the very least, if not impossible.

> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/manage-users-with-computer-management-and-group-policy?u=76281980&t=138)** Perhaps in the case of a home network or a very small business with one user that needs specific limitations search for MMC.exe and click it in the results.

#### Use Group Policy to secure users and computers
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Did you know that you can log in to your Windows PC with something other than a traditional password?
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980&t=6)** You can choose a PIN or use a picture password, if you'd rather.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980&t=10)** Both are better choices on tablets because they require you only type a few numbers or use your finger to draw three gestures on an image.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980&t=18)** You can opt to lock the screen after a specific amount of time passes and require a password when you wake it up, as well.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980&t=25)** You do all of these things from Start and Settings.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980&t=30)** To configure login options, click Accounts.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980&t=34)** Click Sign-in options.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980&t=37)** If you choose PIN, you just click add.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980&t=42)** Type your password, and type and confirm your new PIN.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980&t=49)** You can change your password here, and here you can add a picture password.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980&t=54)** Same thing, type your password, and choose a picture.
>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980&t=59)** This is the one I selected, but you'll probably opt to choose a new picture, and then choose one you have saved to your computer.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980&t=67)** At the top of this screen, you can change when to require a sign-in.
>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980&t=72)** By default, you'll have to type a password or PIN or use your picture password every time you wake the computer from sleep.
>
> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980&t=82)** You can turn that off, though.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980&t=84)** I don't suggest it.
>
> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980&t=86)** If you do choose to set the computer to require a password after it wakes from sleep here in Settings, you want to set how long the computer should be idle before it goes to sleep.
>
> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980&t=96)** To set that, click back and open System.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980&t=101)** Here's where you can tell Windows when to turn off the screen or go to sleep.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980&t=106)** You do that from the Power and Sleep tab.
>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980&t=110)** I have mine set like this.
>
> **[1:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980&t=112)** Turn the screen off after 10 minutes, but when plugged in, never put the computer to sleep.
>
> **[1:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980&t=119)** That's because I work at it all the time, and I'm always near it.
>
> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980&t=124)** Passwords and requiring them are extremely important when securing your computer and the computers on your network.
>
> **[2:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980&t=131)** That said, while you can tell your computers to create passwords and perhaps even change them once a month, you can't force them to without setting group policies.
>
> **[2:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980&t=142)** You can open the local group policy editor by typing gpedit.msc in the task bar.
>
> **[2:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980&t=150)** I've already done that, and I have it open.
>
> **[2:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980&t=153)** To access the password settings, navigate to Computer Configuration, Windows Settings, Security Settings, Account Policies, and here is Password Policy.
>
> **[2:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980&t=166)** Let's take a look at these one at a time.
>
> **[2:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980&t=169)** The maximum password age setting let you configure how many days can pass before the user is required to change their password.
>
> **[2:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980&t=178)** You can set passwords to expire after a number of days between one and 999, or you can specify that passwords never expire by setting the number of days to zero.
>
> **[3:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980&t=190)** Often, administrators choose 30 days or 60 days, but the choice is up to you.
>
> **[3:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980&t=197)** The Enforce Password History Policy setting let you set the number of unique new passwords that must be associated with the user account before an older password can be used.
>
> **[3:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980&t=208)** If you enable Enforce Password History, you should also configure a minimum password age.
>
> **[3:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980&t=215)** Minimum password age states how long a user must keep their password before it can be changed.
>
> **[3:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980&t=221)** If you don't configure this setting, users can change their password as many times in a row as necessary when they're required to, and then reuse their original password.
>
> **[3:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980&t=233)** The minimum password length policy lets you set the least number of characters that can make up a password.
>
> **[3:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980&t=239)** You can set a value between one and 14.
>
> **[4:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980&t=243)** If you choose zero, it means no password is required.
>
> **[4:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980&t=246)** The passwords must meet complexity requirements determines whether passwords must meet certain standards.
>
> **[4:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980&t=254)** Those standards are listed here, and include the following.
>
> **[4:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980&t=258)** Passwords cannot contain the user's account name or parts of the user's full name that exceed two consecutive characters.
>
> **[4:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980&t=265)** And passwords must be at least six characters in length.
>
> **[4:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980&t=269)** They must contain characters from three of the following four categories, uppercase characters A through Z, lowercase characters A through Z, numbers, and special characters like exclamation points and dollar signs.
>
> **[4:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980&t=286)** Finally, the Store Password Using Reversible Encryption Setting provides support for applications that use protocols that require the user's password for authentication.
>
> **[4:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980&t=296)** Reversible means that the encrypted passwords can be decrypted.
>
> **[5:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980&t=301)** An attacker who is able to break this encryption can access available resources.
>
> **[5:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980&t=306)** You should never enable this policy setting unless the application requirements outweigh the need to protect password information.
>
> **[5:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980&t=314)** You can incorporate account lockout policies with the password policy settings you configure.
>
> **[5:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980&t=319)** This lets you state when and how a user will be locked out of their computer if they try to input their password several times, but fail.
>
> **[5:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980&t=328)** If you're interested in that, take a few minutes to review those entries.
>
> **[5:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980&t=332)** Here's the account lockout duration, threshold, and an account lockout counter.
>
> **[5:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980&t=339)** As an example, you can set an account threshold for invalid logon attempts, say six, and then set how long to keep the user locked out before they can try again.
>
> **[5:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980&t=350)** You can also set how much time must pass before resetting the account lockout counter.
>
> **[5:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980&t=356)** So that's about it for password security and password policies.
>
> **[5:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980&t=359)** Remember, whatever you configure here is applied to the entire computer.
>
> **[6:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/use-group-policy-to-secure-users-and-computers?u=76281980&t=364)** If you change your mind about it, come back and remove the policies you don't like.

### 4. Configure System and Data Recovery

#### Recover Windows 10 with a recovery drive
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/recover-windows-10-with-a-recovery-drive?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/recover-windows-10-with-a-recovery-drive?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] When Windows encounters a catastrophic failure, one that is so bad you can't boot the machine to access the recovery options from inside the operating system, you can use your recovery drive to get the computer back up and running.
>
> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/recover-windows-10-with-a-recovery-drive?u=76281980&t=13)** You have to create this drive yourself, though, before a problem occurs.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/recover-windows-10-with-a-recovery-drive?u=76281980&t=17)** So if you haven't done it yet, now's a good a time as any.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/recover-windows-10-with-a-recovery-drive?u=76281980&t=21)** To get started, type recovery drive in the search area of the task bar and click it in the results.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/recover-windows-10-with-a-recovery-drive?u=76281980&t=27)** I've already done that and I've selected Recovery Drive app.
>

>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/recover-windows-10-with-a-recovery-drive?u=76281980&t=43)** What it doesn't say is that you need to insert a USB stick that holds at least eight gigabyte of data and that any existing data on it will be erased.
>

>
> **[0:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/recover-windows-10-with-a-recovery-drive?u=76281980&t=57)** Make sure that Back up system files to the recovery drive is selected and then click Next.
>
> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/recover-windows-10-with-a-recovery-drive?u=76281980&t=66)** Wait while Windows looks for a drive to use.
>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/recover-windows-10-with-a-recovery-drive?u=76281980&t=69)** This could take a minute or two.

>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/recover-windows-10-with-a-recovery-drive?u=76281980&t=79)** Note that everything on the drive will be deleted, so if you have any personal files on it, you'll need to make sure those have been backed up before you click Create.
>
> **[1:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/recover-windows-10-with-a-recovery-drive?u=76281980&t=88)** When you're ready, click Create.
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/recover-windows-10-with-a-recovery-drive?u=76281980&t=92)** It might take an hour or more, so you might want to find something else to do for awhile.
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/recover-windows-10-with-a-recovery-drive?u=76281980&t=97)** Once it finishes, click Finish, and then clearly mark the recovery drive on it and store the USB drive in a safe place.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/recover-windows-10-with-a-recovery-drive?u=76281980&t=106)** If you ever find yourself in a situation where the computer won't boot, all you have to do is insert this drive and try again.
>
> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/recover-windows-10-with-a-recovery-drive?u=76281980&t=113)** The computer will likely boot right to the drive.
>
> **[1:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/recover-windows-10-with-a-recovery-drive?u=76281980&t=116)** Troubleshooting options should appear.
>
> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/recover-windows-10-with-a-recovery-drive?u=76281980&t=118)** You can try automatic repair and if that doesn't work, system restore.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/recover-windows-10-with-a-recovery-drive?u=76281980&t=123)** If you still can't get the computer to start up, choose system image recovery.
>
> **[2:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/recover-windows-10-with-a-recovery-drive?u=76281980&t=128)** Before you move on, do you have any other computers you manage?
>
> **[2:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/recover-windows-10-with-a-recovery-drive?u=76281980&t=131)** Consider making recovery disks for those computers, too, or at the very least, verify system restore is enabled and backups are in place.

#### Create and manage System Restore points
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/create-and-manage-system-restore-points?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/create-and-manage-system-restore-points?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] System Restore has been a part of Windows since Windows ME, and automatically takes snapshots of the operating system and its various components, including the registry without input from you.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/create-and-manage-system-restore-points?u=76281980&t=11)** That is, as long as System Restore's enabled.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/create-and-manage-system-restore-points?u=76281980&t=14)** The snapshots it saves are called restore points.
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/create-and-manage-system-restore-points?u=76281980&t=19)** You can get to System Properties here by typing "system restore" in a search bar, and clicking Create a restore point in the results.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/create-and-manage-system-restore-points?u=76281980&t=28)** If there ever comes a time when the computer begins to perform poorly, you can use these restore points to recover the system to a time that it was stable.
>
> **[0:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/create-and-manage-system-restore-points?u=76281980&t=36)** Notice that System Restore only restores the operating system and the registry.
>
> **[0:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/create-and-manage-system-restore-points?u=76281980&t=41)** It will not make any changes to your files, pictures, music, downloads, videos, and other personal data.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/create-and-manage-system-restore-points?u=76281980&t=49)** Notice here that C is listed and the protection is on.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/create-and-manage-system-restore-points?u=76281980&t=54)** C is usually the drive we're concerned with, although other drives can certainly exist and contain data.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/create-and-manage-system-restore-points?u=76281980&t=60)** V holds my virtual machines and protection is turned off.
>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/create-and-manage-system-restore-points?u=76281980&t=64)** If you ever feel like you're about to do something risky, perhaps installing a new device or device driver, you can create a restore point yourself.
>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/create-and-manage-system-restore-points?u=76281980&t=72)** Click Create to create one now.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/create-and-manage-system-restore-points?u=76281980&t=76)** I'll type a description and I'll click Create.
>
> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/create-and-manage-system-restore-points?u=76281980&t=82)** When you see this prompt, click Close.
>
> **[1:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/create-and-manage-system-restore-points?u=76281980&t=85)** To see the new restore point and learn how to restore from it, click System Restore.
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/create-and-manage-system-restore-points?u=76281980&t=92)** Click Next to get started.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/create-and-manage-system-restore-points?u=76281980&t=94)** You can choose the point you just created, or if others exist, you can choose from them as well.
>
> **[1:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/create-and-manage-system-restore-points?u=76281980&t=100)** You can also scan for affected programs. I'll click Next.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/create-and-manage-system-restore-points?u=76281980&t=105)** If you click Finish here, the computer will start the restore process and will reboot.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/create-and-manage-system-restore-points?u=76281980&t=111)** It'll take some time as well, perhaps 10 to 15 minutes, maybe longer.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/create-and-manage-system-restore-points?u=76281980&t=115)** So don't do that now. Let's click Cancel.
>
> **[1:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/create-and-manage-system-restore-points?u=76281980&t=119)** To make sure System Restore is set up correctly, click Configure.
>
> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/create-and-manage-system-restore-points?u=76281980&t=124)** Note how much disk space you have allotted for System Restore.
>
> **[2:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/create-and-manage-system-restore-points?u=76281980&t=128)** I suggest keeping it at around 15 or 20%, provided you have the free space you need on your drive to allow for that much space to be used.
>
> **[2:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/create-and-manage-system-restore-points?u=76281980&t=137)** The number of restore points you'll have to choose from depends on your computer configuration.
>
> **[2:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/create-and-manage-system-restore-points?u=76281980&t=142)** The more space you give to System Restore, the more restore points you'll have.
>
> **[2:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/create-and-manage-system-restore-points?u=76281980&t=147)** As the allotted spaces fill, the oldest restore points will be deleted and new ones will take their place.
>
> **[2:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/create-and-manage-system-restore-points?u=76281980&t=153)** Let's cancel out of this and let's look at some Group Policy settings for System Restore.
>
> **[2:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/create-and-manage-system-restore-points?u=76281980&t=159)** I'll type "gpedit.msc" I'll type "gpedit.msc" I'll type "gpedit.msc" and we'll have a look.
>
> **[2:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/create-and-manage-system-restore-points?u=76281980&t=169)** From Computer Configuration, expand Administrative Templates, and then System.
>
> **[2:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/create-and-manage-system-restore-points?u=76281980&t=178)** Scroll down to System Restore.

> **[3:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/create-and-manage-system-restore-points?u=76281980&t=182)** There are two options: One is to turn off Configuration options, and another is to turn off System Restore completely.
>
> **[3:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/create-and-manage-system-restore-points?u=76281980&t=190)** I see no reason to disable System Restore.
>
> **[3:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/create-and-manage-system-restore-points?u=76281980&t=192)** Although I could see reasons for disabling the options.
>

>

#### Explore recovery options
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/explore-recovery-options?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/explore-recovery-options?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Sometimes there's nothing you can do to get an unstable computer in good working order again, no matter how hard you try.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/explore-recovery-options?u=76281980&t=7)** When you come to this realization, you'll want to explore the recovery options.
>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/explore-recovery-options?u=76281980&t=12)** Click Start, Settings, Update & Security, and Recovery.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/explore-recovery-options?u=76281980&t=20)** You can reset the PC, perhaps go back to a previous version of Windows, or access Advanced startup options.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/explore-recovery-options?u=76281980&t=28)** Resetting the PC re-installs the Windows operating system, which fixes problems that have to do with Windows.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/explore-recovery-options?u=76281980&t=35)** Sometimes operating system files get corrupt or go missing and reinstalling them is you only way to repair them.
>
> **[0:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/explore-recovery-options?u=76281980&t=45)** This process will also uninstall applications, though.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/explore-recovery-options?u=76281980&t=49)** It's important to do this because oftentimes it's those pesky third-party apps that caused system instability.
>
> **[0:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/explore-recovery-options?u=76281980&t=55)** Removing these can resolve problems that no other method can.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/explore-recovery-options?u=76281980&t=60)** Read the two choices carefully.
>
> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/explore-recovery-options?u=76281980&t=63)** You can opt to keep your files or remove them.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/explore-recovery-options?u=76281980&t=67)** Make sure to back up files and folders, no matter what choice you make, though, just in case something goes awry.
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/explore-recovery-options?u=76281980&t=73)** If you want to sell your computer or give it to someone else, choose the second option.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/explore-recovery-options?u=76281980&t=78)** Definitely want to remove all your files.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/explore-recovery-options?u=76281980&t=81)** Otherwise, opt for the basic reset.
>
> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/explore-recovery-options?u=76281980&t=86)** The second choice here is to go back to a previous version of Windows.
>
> **[1:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/explore-recovery-options?u=76281980&t=90)** Notice it's no longer an option on my PC because it was updated more than 10 days ago.
>
> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/explore-recovery-options?u=76281980&t=96)** If you're having extremely difficult problems with the computer, you'll need to choose Advanced startup.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/explore-recovery-options?u=76281980&t=101)** This lets you start a device from a disk, like a USB drive or DVD.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/explore-recovery-options?u=76281980&t=106)** You can change your firmware settings, too, or change Windows startup settings.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/explore-recovery-options?u=76281980&t=111)** You can even restore from a system image.
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/explore-recovery-options?u=76281980&t=114)** This will return your computer to a time when it was brand new, though, or from an image that you created not too long ago.
>
> **[2:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/explore-recovery-options?u=76281980&t=121)** Whatever the case, there's likely one option that will work for you here, good luck.

> **[3:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/troubleshoot-the-startup-and-boot-process?u=76281980&t=237)** This might entail navigating to a Recovery Drive, running a Repair sequence, booting into Safe Mode, and more.

#### Recover the OS with Windows Recovery Environment
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/recover-the-os-with-windows-recovery-environment?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/recover-the-os-with-windows-recovery-environment?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Technician] The Windows Recovery Environment also called Windows RE contains automatic repair tools that may be able to help you recover the system after a computer failure.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/recover-the-os-with-windows-recovery-environment?u=76281980&t=11)** Windows RE, also contains options for administrators and tech specialists, such as access to the command prompt, the ability to recover using a system image disc and options to access the firmware for UEFI settings among other things.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/recover-the-os-with-windows-recovery-environment?u=76281980&t=26)** You may be able to boot to the recovery environment from settings, recovery, and advanced options if your computer configuration supports it.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/recover-the-os-with-windows-recovery-environment?u=76281980&t=34)** There are other ways to enter the RE environment; you can hold down the shift key while you click restart to reboot the computer.
>
> **[0:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/recover-the-os-with-windows-recovery-environment?u=76281980&t=41)** You can use settings mentioned earlier or you can boot using recovery media like a recovery disk.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/recover-the-os-with-windows-recovery-environment?u=76281980&t=49)** I prefer to use a physical disk myself because most computers are already configured to boot to the disc automatically and will do so without difficulty.
>
> **[0:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/recover-the-os-with-windows-recovery-environment?u=76281980&t=57)** Windows RE will automatically start in certain instances too for example after two consecutive failed boot attempts or two unexpected shutdowns that occur within two minutes of boot completion, you'll see the RE environment.
>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/recover-the-os-with-windows-recovery-environment?u=76281980&t=72)** It will also happen when the computer encounters a secure boot error on any computer or a Bit Locker error on touch devices.
>
> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/recover-the-os-with-windows-recovery-environment?u=76281980&t=80)** When you get to the recovery environment what you see, depends on your computer setup.
>
> **[1:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/recover-the-os-with-windows-recovery-environment?u=76281980&t=85)** If you have devices connected that windows recognizes like USB drives and DVD drives, you'll see an option named "User Device".
>
> **[1:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/recover-the-os-with-windows-recovery-environment?u=76281980&t=93)** We don't have that option here, but if you do, you can select it and choose the device to boot to.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/recover-the-os-with-windows-recovery-environment?u=76281980&t=99)** You'll see this option, if you've already inserted a recovery disk or system image disk too.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/recover-the-os-with-windows-recovery-environment?u=76281980&t=105)** But what I'd like to show you here are the options under troubleshoot.
>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/recover-the-os-with-windows-recovery-environment?u=76281980&t=108)** You're probably familiar with some of these tools.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/recover-the-os-with-windows-recovery-environment?u=76281980&t=111)** System Restore, let's you choose a restore point.
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/recover-the-os-with-windows-recovery-environment?u=76281980&t=114)** This will enable you to return your computer to a stable state when perhaps only a few days passed.
>
> **[2:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/recover-the-os-with-windows-recovery-environment?u=76281980&t=121)** Another good choice is Startup Repair.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/recover-the-os-with-windows-recovery-environment?u=76281980&t=123)** With this option the startup files are restored and repaired and problems with startup can be resolved quite easily.
>
> **[2:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/recover-the-os-with-windows-recovery-environment?u=76281980&t=130)** You can also change startup settings if you see the option, you can enable safe mode for instance or disable automatic restart on system failures.
>
> **[2:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/recover-the-os-with-windows-recovery-environment?u=76281980&t=139)** If you believe you can resolve a problem yourself, say by using safe mode or by uninstalling new device drivers or recently installed programs, this could be a good option for you.
>
> **[2:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/recover-the-os-with-windows-recovery-environment?u=76281980&t=149)** "System Image Recovery" is another option.
>
> **[2:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/recover-the-os-with-windows-recovery-environment?u=76281980&t=152)** If you have a system image disc that isn't too old assistant image disc is like a picture of the system state.
>
> **[2:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/recover-the-os-with-windows-recovery-environment?u=76281980&t=158)** You can also access UEFI firmware settings if you have that sort of system.
>
> **[2:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/recover-the-os-with-windows-recovery-environment?u=76281980&t=163)** So that leaves the command prompt.
>
> **[2:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/recover-the-os-with-windows-recovery-environment?u=76281980&t=165)** If you're good here, perhaps with knowledge of command line tools such as VCD edit and BCD boot, this might be a good option for you.
>
> **[2:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/recover-the-os-with-windows-recovery-environment?u=76281980&t=174)** Finally, there's a new option to go back to the previous build.
>
> **[2:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/recover-the-os-with-windows-recovery-environment?u=76281980&t=178)** I think this will become a popular option as Windows updates and upgrades become more fluid when Windows is just Windows and is no longer Windows 7, 8 or 10.
>
> **[3:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/recover-the-os-with-windows-recovery-environment?u=76281980&t=188)** with this option, you'll be able to undo an upgrade if you have problems with it.
>
> **[3:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/recover-the-os-with-windows-recovery-environment?u=76281980&t=192)** So think about the problem you're having before you make a choice.
>
> **[3:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/recover-the-os-with-windows-recovery-environment?u=76281980&t=196)** If it's a recent problem system restore might work fine.
>
> **[3:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/recover-the-os-with-windows-recovery-environment?u=76281980&t=199)** If it's a startup issue, try Startup Repair.
>
> **[3:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/recover-the-os-with-windows-recovery-environment?u=76281980&t=203)** Assistant Image Recovery Disk if available is also a good choice.
>
> **[3:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/windows-10-manage-and-maintain-windows-10-2019/recover-the-os-with-windows-recovery-environment?u=76281980&t=207)** Make sure to consider all angles and then click the desired option to work through whatever process is required.
